        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have emerged as a promising candidate for large-scale stationary energy storage in light of possible concerns over cost and abundance.  Advanced sodium host materials are required for developing SIBs with high energy d., long cycling stability and high safety.  Layered metal dichalcogenides (MX2, M = Mo, W, Sn, V, Ti; X = S, Se, Te) have become a hot spot for anode materials in SIBs due to their merits of high cond., mech. and thermal stability and structural stability.  In this review, we first present a comprehensive overview of the progress of layered MX2 anodes for SIBs.  Detailed discussion on the advantages of MX2 as SIB anodes is then made.  Emphasis is placed on enhancing the electrochem. performance through nanostructure engineering, crystal structure modulation, doping/alloying and composite design.  We conclude with a perspective on the further development of SIBs in view of their applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqJtS76pRrKJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhw2BizJhtwFA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXksFCksrs%253D&amp;md5=937107c9b1a2d8e6950bcbe9c948edd3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1039/C9TA09636A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Layer-by-Layer Stacked Nanohybrids of N,S-co-Doped Carbon Film Modified Stomic MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets for Advanced Sodium Dual-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layer-by-layer stacked nanohybrids of N,S-co-doped carbon film modified atomic MoS2 nanosheets for advanced sodium dual-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, YangJie; Hu, Xiang; Zhong, Guobao; Chen, Junxiang; Zhan, Hongbing; Wen, Zhenhai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">24271-24280</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium dual-ion batteries (SDIBs) have received tremendous research attention due to their multiple advantages of environmental friendliness and high working voltages.  However, the development of high-performance SDIBs still remains a daunting challenge, mainly due to the lack of robust anode materials with sufficient interlayer spacing for Na+ insertion/extn.  We here report a solvothermal method for the fabrication of coral-like nanohybrids that are constructed from layer-by-layer stacked nitrogen and sulfur co-doped carbon film modified at. MoS2 nanosheets (a-MoS2NS@NSCfilm).  Comprehensive characterization demonstrates that a-MoS2NS@NSCfilm shows favorable electrochem. and structural properties for sodium ion storage, including significantly improved elec. cond. and an expanded layer space of 0.95 nm thanks to carbon film modification, which favorably facilitate electron transfer and enhance Na+ diffusion kinetics, thus leading to an impressive capability for fast and high-capacity sodium storage.  We further verify the practical application of a-MoS2NS@NSCfilm as an anode for SDIBs by coupling it with an expanded graphite (EG) cathode; this delivers a capacity of 40 mA h g-1 with outstanding cycling stability and an extremely low capacity decay of 0.0056% per cycle after 5000 cycles at 10C.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIcLN-7h2eOLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhw2BizJhtwFA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical MoS2/Carbon Composite Microspheres as Advanced Anodes for Lithium/Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tang, Wangjia; Wang, Xiuli; Zhong, Yu; Xie, Dong; Zhang, Xuqing; Xia, Xinhui; Wu, Jiangbo; Gu, Changdong; Tu, Jiangping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">24</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">43</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11220-11226</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CEUJED</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0947-6539</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is crucial to design advanced electrodes with large Li/Na-ion storage capacities for the development of next-generation battery systems.  Herein, hierarchical MoS2/C composite microspheres were constructed by facile template-free self-assembly sulfurization plus post-carbonization.  Cross-linked MoS2 nanosheets and outer carbon layer are organically combined together to form composite microspheres with diams. of 400-500 nm.  Due to enhanced elec. cond. and good structural stability, the MoS2/C composite microspheres exhibit substantially improved Li/Na-ion storage performance.  Compared to unmodified MoS2, MoS2/C composite microspheres deliver higher Li/Na-ion storage capacity (Li+: 1017 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and Na+: 531 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1), as well as better rate capability (Li+: 434 mA h g-1 at 1 Ag-1 and Na+: 102 mA h g-1 at 1 Ag-1) and capacity retention (Li+: 902 mA h g-1 after 200 cycles and Na+: 342 mA h g-1 over 100 cycles).  The superior Li/Na-ion storage performance is mainly attributed to the unique porous microsphere architecture with increased electrode/electrolyte interfaces and more diffusion paths for Li/Na ion insertion.  Addnl., the carbon coating can not only improve the electronic cond., but also suppress the shuttle effect of polysulfides.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrJFKLWsUa2P7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhw2BizJhtwFA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXht1KqtLbP&amp;md5=27e7cc1b4389c606686814c8bcec8abe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201800658"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Controllable Design of MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets Anchored on Nitrogen-Doped Graphene: Toward Fast Sodium Storage by Tunable Pseudocapacitance</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Densified MoS2/Ti3C2 films with balanced porosity for ultrahigh volumetric capacity sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ma, Kun; Dong, Yuru; Jiang, Hao; Hu, Yanjie; Saha, Petr; Li, Chunzhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">413</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">127479</span>CODEN:

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing high volumetric energy d. sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is indispensable for catering to the miniaturization and flexibility of various consumer electronics.  Herein, we have reported the flexible and compact MoS2/Ti3C2 hybrid films with balanced porosity, where the few-layered MoS2 nanosheets are parallelly intercalated into the Ti3C2 interlayer space in virtue of strong electrostatic effect and difference in their sizes.  The hybrid films have been stabilized by the two-dimensional (2D) confinement effect and the Ti-S-Mo bonds with a high d. of ∼2.9 g cm-3.  Furthermore, the dual 2D compds. intrinsically possess satisfied ions cond., and meanwhile give rapid electrons transfer after assembling such superstructure.  When directly used as SIB anode, the MoS2/Ti3C2 hybrid films deliver an exceptional volumetric specific capacity of 1510 mAh cm-3 at 0.28 mA cm-2 and 650 mAh cm-3 at 14 mA cm-2.  The specific capacity remains unchanged after 300 cycles at 1.4 mA cm-2.  More significantly, the areal specific capacity shows a linear relationship with the increase of film thickness from 9.6 to 43.1μm without sacrificing the volumetric capacity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoYDLNy80EWA7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhw2BizJhtwFA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Covalent Assembly of MoS2 Nanosheets with SnS Nanodots as Linkages for Lithium/Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ru, Jiajia; He, Ting; Chen, Binjie; Feng, Yutong; Zu, Lianhai; Wang, Zhijun; Zhang, Qiaobao; Hao, Tianzi; Meng, Ruijin; Che, Renchao; Zhang, Chi; Yang, Jinhu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Weak van der Waals interactions between interlayers of two-dimensional layered materials result in disabled across-interlayer electron transfer and poor layered structural stability, seriously deteriorating their performance in energy applications.  Herein, we propose a novel covalent assembly strategy for MoS2 nanosheets to realize unique MoS2/SnS hollow superassemblies (HSs) by using SnS nanodots as covalent linkages.  The covalent assembly based on all-inorg. and carbon-free concept enables effective across-interlayer electron transfer, facilitated ion diffusion kinetics, and outstanding mech. stability, which are evidenced by exptl. characterization, DFT calcns., and mech. simulations.  Consequently, the MoS2/SnS HSs exhibit superb rate performance and long cycling stability in lithium-ion batteries, representing the best comprehensive performance in carbon-free MoS2-based anodes to date.  Moreover, the MoS2/SnS HSs also show excellent sodium storage performance in sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGomlBu6zto2wLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg6_KjEe_pCbw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtlShtrjE&amp;md5=63db1ad44bd29627da30a96091b5be98</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2019.227271"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In-Situ Growth of Vertically Aligned MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanowalls on Reduced Graphene Oxide Enables A Large Capacity and Highly Stable Anode for Sodium Ion Storage</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In-situ growth of vertically aligned MoS2 nanowalls on reduced graphene oxide enables a large capacity and highly stable anode for sodium ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Hai; Song, Tianbing; Tang, Linbin; Pu, Xiaoming; Li, Zhi; Xu, Qunjie; Liu, Haimei; Wang, YongGang; Xia, Yongyao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2 has attracted remarkable attention, attributed to its high specific capacity and graphite-like structure.  However, the low rate capability and poor cycle stability are two major obstacles that hinder the practical application of MoS2 in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, MoS2 grows vertically on the surface of reduced graphene oxide (rGO) and forms a nanowall structure by electrostatic attraction, whose growth has been induced by cetyltrimethyl ammonium bromide (CTAB).  This unique nanowall has a large sp. surface area, which not only exposes plenty of active sites and shortens the diffusion distance of Na+, but also improves the electronic cond. and structural stability.  Meanwhile, detailed kinetic anal. is also employed to explain the Na+ storage behavior.  The pseudo capacitance-dominated contribution ensures a more stable and much faster Na+ storage.  Therefore, the MoS2@rGO composite displays excellent electrochem. performance.  For example, the capacity of the MoS2@rGO composite can still be maintained at 571.5 mA h g-1 with 94.1% retention, after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1.  Impressively, MoS2@rGO still exhibits a considerable capacity of 124 mA h g-1 at an ultra-high c.d. of 40 A g-1.  The excellent performance makes the MoS2@rGO material a prospective electrode for use in large-scale SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpOHldK2V9JF7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg6_KjEe_pCbw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitVygt7zF&amp;md5=13c471c0dc7b28d1b24abb1fee2eb882</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.9b21365"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchically Porous MoS<sub>2</sub>–Carbon Hollow Rhomboids for Superior Performance of The Anode of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchically Porous MoS2-Carbon Hollow Rhomboids for Superior Performance of the Anode of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han Lifeng; Zhang Li; Cao Shaokui; Han Lifeng; Wu Shide; Wang Shiwen; Zhang Yong; Guo Dongjie; Hu Zhe; Chen Mingzhe; Ding Junwei; Chou Shulei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS applied materials &amp; interfaces</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">It is always challenging to fabricate two-dimensional transition-metal dichalcogenides into multiple hollow micro-/nanostructures with improved properties for various potential applications.  Here, hierarchically porous MoS2-C hollow rhomboids (MCHRs) have been creatively synthesized via a facile self-templated solvothermal approach.  It has been clarified that the obtained MCHRs assembled beneath ultrathin γ-MnS and carbon cohybridized MoS2 nanosheets under the structural direction of the MnMoO4·0.49H2O self-template.  The prepared MCHR anode of sodium-ion batteries exhibited a reversible capacity of 506 mA h g(-1) at 0.1 A g(-1), ultrahigh rate capabilities up to 10 A g(-1) with 310 mA h g(-1), and exceptional stability over 3000 cycles.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal-Semiconductor Phase Twinned Hierarchical MoS2 Nanowires with Expanded Interlayers for Sodium-Ion Batteries with Ultralong Cycle Life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ye, Wei; Wu, Fangfang; Shi, Nianxiang; Zhou, Han; Chi, Qianqian; Chen, Weihua; Du, Shiyu; Gao, Peng; Li, Haibo; Xiong, Shenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered a prospective candidate for large-scale energy storage due to the merits of abundant sodium resources and low cost.  However, a lack of suitable advanced anode materials has hindered further applications.  Herein, metal-semiconductor mixed phase twinned hierarchical (MPTH) MoS2 nanowires with an expanded interlayer (9.63 Å) are engineered and prepd. using MoO3 nanobelts as a self-sacrificed template in the presence of a trace amt. of (NH4)6Mo7O24·4H2O as initiator.  The greatly expanded interlayer spacing accelerates Na+ insertion/extn. kinetics, and the metal-semiconductor mixed phase enhances electron transfer ability and stabilizes electrode structure during cycling.  Benefiting from the structural merits, the MPTH MoS2 electrode delivers high reversible capacities of 200 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 for 200 cycles and 154 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 for 2450 cycles in the voltage range of 0.4-3.0 V.  Strikingly, the electrode maintains 6500 cycles at a c.d. of 2 A g-1, corresponding to a capacity retention of 82.8% of the 2nd cycle, overwhelming the all reported MoS2 cycling results.  This study provides an alternative strategy to boost SIB cycling performance in terms of reversible capacity by virtue of interlayer expansion and structure stability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGppq1pGfamQ6LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg6_KjEe_pCbw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sacrificial template synthesis of hollow C@MoS2@PPy nanocomposites as anodes for enhanced sodium storage performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Guangming; Bi, Xuanxuan; Yue, Hailong; Jin, Rencheng; Wang, Qingyao; Gao, Shanmin; Lu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) has become a potential anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) by showing decent cell performance but it suffers poor electronic cond. and large vol. expansion during sodiation.  Here we design a nanocomposite with hollow nitrogen doped carbon and polypyrrole modified MoS2 for improving the performance for SIBs.  The designed nanocomposite shows a much-improved electronic cond. and the design of the architecture provides sufficient channels for mass transport and accommodates large vol. change.  This C@MoS2@PPy anode delivers a high specific capacity of 713 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 for 100 cycles, and an excellent rate capacity of 294 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 for 500 cycles.  This specific architecture of C@MoS2@PPy could guide the future design of the electrode material in SIBs and its superior electrochem. performance indicates the great potential application for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqL7q-RYIfwWLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg6_KjEe_pCbw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sub-Millimeter-Scale Monolayer p-Type H-Phase VS2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Su, Jianwei; Wang, Mingshan; Li, Yuan; Wang, Fakun; Chen, Qiao; Luo, Peng; Han, Junbo; Wang, Shun; Li, Huiqiao; Zhai, Tianyou</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">30</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2000240</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">2D H-phase vanadium disulfide (VS2) is expected to exhibit tunable semiconductor properties as compared with its metallic T-phase structure, and thus is of promise for future electronic applications.  However, to date such 2D H-phase VS2 nanostructures have not been realized in expt. likely due to the polymorphs of vanadium sulfides and thermodn. instability of H-phase VS2.  Prepn. of H-phase VS2 monolayer with lateral size up to 250μm, as a new member in the 2D transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) family, is reported.  A unique growth environment is built by introducing the molten salt-mediated precursor system as well as the epitaxial mica growth platform, which successfully overcomes the aforementioned growth challenges and enables the evolution of 2D H-phase structure of VS2.  The honeycomb-like structure of H-phase VS2 with broken inversion symmetry is confirmed by spherical aberration-cor. scanning transmission electron microscopy and second harmonic generation characterization.  The phase structure is found to be ultra-stable up to 500 K.  The field-effect device study further demonstrates the p-type semiconducting nature of the 2D H-phase VS2.  The study introduces a new phase-stable 2D TMDs materials with potential features for future electronic devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoLzDpBAZpWhLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljMPIFQ3qC3HQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXktVeqsrw%253D&amp;md5=af21f5e9542dd3df788586ded6539ded</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1002/ange.201912756"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Accurate Control of VS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets for Coexisting High Photoluminescence and Photothermal Conversion Efficiency</span>. <i>Angew.                             cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2018.07.036"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nano-Grain Dependent 3D Hierarchical VS<sub>2</sub> Microrods with Enhanced Intercalation Kinetic for Sodium Storage Properties</span>. <i>J. Power Sources</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>398</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">91</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">98</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2018.07.036</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D398%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D91-98%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DW.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BHuang%26author%3DL.%2BFeng%26author%3DL.%2BCao%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DL.%2BPan%26title%3DNano-Grain%2BDependent%2B3D%2BHierarchical%2BVS2%2BMicrorods%2Bwith%2BEnhanced%2BIntercalation%2BKinetic%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BStorage%2BProperties%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2018.07.036&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c05096&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2018.07.036&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nano-grain dependent 3D hierarchical VS2 microrods with enhanced intercalation kinetic for sodium storage properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Wenbin; Huang, Jianfeng; Feng, Liangliang; Cao, Liyun; Liu, Yijun; Pan, Limin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">398</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">91-98</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Construction of well-defined three-dimensional (3D) assembled architectures is an effective strategy to improve the electrochem. reaction kinetics of sodium-ion storage.  Herein, 3D hierarchical VS2 microrods assembled by nanosheets comprised of small VS2 nano-grains are controllably synthesized by a facile in-situ chem. etching approach.  Results show that the addn. amt. of ethanol serving as the etching agent has a great influence on the oriented growth and size (thickness-to-diam. ratio) of VS2 nano-grains.  Moreover, (001)-oriented VS2 nano-grains with larger thickness-to-diam. ratio expose more layer-edges and unsatd. S-edges, and then dramatically improve the intercalation kinetic, eventually leading to the enhancement of rate performance and cycling capacity.  When applied as anode for sodium ion batteries, this material affords a high capacity of 255 and 230 mAhg-1 even at a high rate of 1.0 and 2.0 A g-1, and a reversible capacity of 350 mAhg-1 is still achieved after the following cycling test of 200 cycles at 0.2 A g-1.  The controllability and simplicity of the in-situ chem. etching approach, combined with the superior sodium storage properties present a promising strategy for the development of versatile synthesis techniques for energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqcbVWMeCKoobVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljMPIFQ3qC3HQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtlenu7jJ&amp;md5=c0d5e242a0dcab4d50824b35e9b72d61</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA03172F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kwok, C.                 10.1039/C7TA03172F</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D15080-15086%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DY.%2BQu%26author%3DM.%2BShao%26author%3DY.%2BShao%26author%3DM.%2BYang%26author%3DJ.%2BXu%26author%3DC.%2BT.%2BKwok%26author%3DX.%2BShi%26author%3DZ.%2BLu%26author%3DH.%2BPan%26title%3DUltra-High%2BElectrocatalytic%2BActivity%2Bof%2BVS2%2BNanoflowers%2Bfor%2BEfficient%2BHydrogen%2BEvolution%2BReaction%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC7TA03172F&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c05096&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC7TA03172F&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultra-high electrocatalytic activity of VS2 nanoflowers for efficient hydrogen evolution reaction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qu, Yuanju; Shao, Mengmeng; Shao, Yangfan; Yang, Mingyang; Xu, Jincheng; Kwok, Chi Tat; Shi, Xingqiang; Lu, Zhouguang; Pan, Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">29</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">15080-15086</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is a great challenge to explore cheap, abundant and eco-friendly electrocatalysts for hydrogen evolution reaction (HER).  Here, we report the fabrication of VS2 nanoflowers with 1T phase by a simple hydrothermal method and their electrocatalytic performance in the HER.  We find that the VS2 nanoflowers show comparable HER performance to Pt in acids, including an ultra-low onset potential of 32 mV, a Tafel slope of 34 mV dec-1 which resembles that of Pt, and a small overpotential of 58 mV (54 mV for Pt) at a c.d. of 10 mA cm-2.  High stability and almost 100% faradaic efficiency indicate the practical application of VS2 nanoflowers in the HER.  Our first-principles calcns. reveal that the thermoneutral Gibbs free energy of hydrogen adsorption on both the basal and edge sites of the 1T-VS2 monolayer can be achieved under certain hydrogen coverage and the monolayer shows good cond., which contribute to the impressive catalytic performance of VS2 nanoflowers.  We expect that the VS2 nanostructures may be applicable in electrocatalysis with high efficiency.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrGzBb6nGOiKbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljMPIFQ3qC3HQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhtVCltbrO&amp;md5=ba1b5903a2f6203869a8bfa56fc108ea</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2020.228282"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Yarn ball-like MoS2 nanospheres coated by nitrogen-doped carbon for enhanced lithium and sodium storage performance</span>. <i>J. Power Sources</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>465</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">228282</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2020.228282</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D465%26publication_year%3D2020%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DJ.%2BBai%26author%3DB.%2BZhao%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DH.%2BMa%26author%3DK.%2BLi%26author%3DZ.%2BFang%26author%3DH.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BDai%26author%3DX.%2BZhu%26author%3DY.%2BSun%26title%3DYarn%2Bball-like%2BMoS2%2Bnanospheres%2Bcoated%2Bby%2Bnitrogen-doped%2Bcarbon%2Bfor%2Benhanced%2Blithium%2Band%2Bsodium%2Bstorage%2Bperformance%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2020.228282&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c05096&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2020.228282&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Yarn ball-like MoS2 nanospheres coated by nitrogen-doped carbon for enhanced lithium and sodium storage performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bai, Jin; Zhao, Bangchuan; Wang, Xin; Ma, Hongyang; Li, Kunzhen; Fang, Zhitang; Li, Han; Dai, Jianming; Zhu, Xuebin; Sun, Yuping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">465</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">228282</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2 has been regarded as one of the most promising anode materials for high-performance lithium-ion (LIBs) or sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its unique two-dimensional (2D) layered structure.  However, the unsatisfied structure stability and poor elec. cond. limit the practical application of MoS2.  Herein, a hierarchical yarn ball-like MoS2 nanosphere structure coated by N-doped carbon layer (MoS2-PVP@NC) is successfully developed to improve the structural stability and elec. cond. of the MoS2 material.  When evaluated as anode material for SIBs, the MoS2-PVP@NC electrode shows an excellent cycling performance of 410.2 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 200 cycles and an ultrahigh rate capability of 352.1 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1.  The composite electrode also presents a high cycling capacity of 607.1 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 300 cycles and high rate performance of 356.0 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1 when used as anode for LIBs.  The excellent electrochem. performance is attributed to the synergetic effect of the yarn ball-like nanosphere structure and the N-doped carbon layer.  This work sheds light on the promising application of the hierarchical MoS2 composite in high-performance lithium-ion or sodium-ion storage system.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq8vbmQlIuUo7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljMPIFQ3qC3HQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXpsFGhs7s%253D&amp;md5=22433ca22e6411d6397e9e7b4dabc51a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36');                 10.1007/s12274-018-2250-2</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D12%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D2218-2223%26journal%3DNano%2BRes.%26author%3DP.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BYang%26author%3DS.%2BGong%26author%3DF.%2BLv%26author%3DW.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DM.%2BLuo%26author%3DY.%2BXing%26author%3DQ.%2BWang%26author%3DS.%2BGuo%26title%3DCo-doped%2B1T-MoS2%2Bnanosheets%2Bembedded%2Bin%2BN%252C%2BS-doped%2Bcarbon%2Bnanobowls%2Bfor%2Bhigh-rate%2Band%2Bultra-stable%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1007%252Fs12274-018-2250-2&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c05096&amp;doiOfLink=10.1007%2Fs12274-018-2250-2&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Co-doped 1T-MoS2 nanosheets embedded in N, S-doped carbon nanobowls for high-rate and ultra-stable sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Peihao; Yang, Yong; Gong, Sheng; Lv, Fan; Wang, Wei; Li, Yiju; Luo, Mingchuan; Xing, Yi; Wang, Qian; Guo, Shaojun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2218-2223</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NRAEB5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1998-0000</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Despite various 2H-MoS2/carbon hybrid nanostructures have been constructed and committed to improve the performance for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), they still show the limited cycle stability due to the relatively large volumetric expansion during the charge-discharge process.  Herein, we report the construction of cobalt-doped few-layered 1T-MoS2 nanosheets embedded in N, S-doped carbon (CMS/NSC) nanobowls derived from metal-org. framework (MOF) precursor via a simple in situ sulfurization process.  This unique hierarchical structure enables the uniformly dispersed Co-doped 1T-MoS2 nanosheets intimately couple with the highly conductive carbon nanobowls, thus efficiently preventing the aggregation.  In particular, the Co-doping plays a crucial role in maintaining the integrity of structure for MoS2 during cycling tests, confirmed by first-principles calcns.  Compared with pristine MoS2, the vol. deformation of Co-doped MoS2 can be shrunk by a prominent value of 52% during cycling.  Furthermore, the few-layered MoS2 nanosheets with 1T metallic phase endow higher cond., and thus can surpass its counterpart 2H semiconducting phase in battery performance.  By virtue of the synergistic effect of stable structure, appropriate doping and high cond., the resulting CMS/NSC hybrid shows superior rate capability and cycle stability.  The capacity of CMS/NSC can still be 235.9 mAh·g-1 even at 25 A·g-1, which is 51.3% of the capacity at 0.2 A·g-1.  Moreover, the capacity can still remain 218.6 mAh·g-1 even over 8,240 cycles at 5 A·g-1 with a low decay of 0.0044% per cycle, one of the best performances among the reported MoS2-based anode materials for SIBs.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Supersaturated bridge-sulfur and vanadium co-doped MoS2 nanosheet arrays with enhanced sodium storage capability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Yuru; Zhu, Zhengju; Hu, Yanjie; He, Guanjie; Sun, Yue; Cheng, Qilin; Parkin, Ivan P.; Jiang, Hao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The low specific capacity and sluggish electrochem. reaction kinetics greatly block the development of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  New high-performance electrode materials will enhance development and are urgently required for SIBs.  Herein, we report the prepn. of supersatd. bridge-sulfur and vanadium co-doped MoS2 nanosheet arrays on carbon cloth (denoted as V-MoS2+x/CC).  The bridge-sulfur in MoS2 has been created as a new active site for greater Na+ storage.  The vanadium doping increases the d. of carriers and facilitates accelerated electron transfer.  The synergistic dual-doping effects endow the V-MoS2+x/CC anodes with high sodium storage performance.  The optimized V-MoS2.49/CC gives superhigh capacities of 370 and 214 mAhU+00B7g-1 at 0.1 and 10 AU+00B7g-1 within 0.4-3.0 V, resp.  After cycling 3,000 times at 2 AU+00B7g-1, almost 83% of the reversible capacity is maintained.  The findings indicate that the electrochem. performances of metal sulfides can be further improved by edge-engineering and lattice-doping co-modification concept.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoJ2MkfRab7brVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-gCY_YiArDw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXitVWqs7jN&amp;md5=0bc49e993837bfd8a0463b59a9d72365</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201900145"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xue, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kong, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">One-Step Synthesis of 2-Ethylhexylamine Pillared Vanadium Disulfide Nanoflowers with Ultralarge Interlayer Spacing for High-Performance Magnesium Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Evolution of the electrochemical interface in sodium ion batteries with ether electrolytes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Kaikai; Zhang, Jun; Lin, Dongmei; Wang, Da-Wei; Li, Baohua; Lv, Wei; Sun, Sheng; He, Yan-Bing; Kang, Feiyu; Yang, Quan-Hong; Zhou, Limin; Zhang, Tong-Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">725</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2041-1723</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Research</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ether based electrolytes have surfaced as alternatives to conventional carbonates allowing for enhanced electrochem. performance of sodium-ion batteries; however, the primary source of the improvement remains poorly understood.  Here we show that coupling titanium dioxide and other anode materials with diglyme does enable higher efficiency and reversible capacity than those for the combination involving ester electrolytes.  Importantly, the electrolyte dependent performance is revealed to be the result of the different structural evolution induced by a varied sodiation depth.  A suit of characterizations show that the energy barrier to charge transfer at the interface between electrolyte and electrode is the factor that dominates the interfacial electrochem. characteristics and therefore the energy storage properties.  Our study proposes a reliable parameter to assess the intricate sodiation dynamics in sodium-ion batteries and could guide the design of aprotic electrolytes for next generation rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp5MBNg2cK80rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-gCY_YiArDw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXns1Gitbk%253D&amp;md5=3f7a4525b81e73f745c4efb6bc980ab3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1021/jp074464w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Polleux, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dunn, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pseudocapacitive Contributions to Electrochemical Energy Storage in TiO<sub>2</sub> (Anatase) Nanoparticles</span>. <i>J. C</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2007</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>111</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">14925</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">14931</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudocapacitive Contributions to Electrochemical Energy Storage in TiO2 (Anatase) Nanoparticles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, John; Polleux, Julien; Lim, James; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2007</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">111</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">40</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14925-14931</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCCCK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1932-7447</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The advantages of using nanostructured materials for electrochem. energy storage have focused on the benefits assocd. with short path lengths.  However, another contribution, capacitive effects which become increasingly important at nanoscale dimensions, was studied.  Nanocryst. TiO2 (anatase) was studied over a dimensional regime where both capacitive and Li intercalation processes contribute to the total stored charge.  An anal. of the voltammetric sweep data was used to distinguish between the amt. of charge stored by these 2 processes.  At particle sizes &lt;10 nm, capacitive contributions became increasingly important, leading to greater amts. of total stored charge (gravimetrically normalized) with decreasing TiO2 particle size.  The area normalized capacitance is well &gt;100 μF/cm2, confirming that the capacitive contribution was pseudocapacitive.  Also, decreasing the particle size to the nanoscale regime led to faster charge/discharge rates because diffusion-controlled Li ion intercalation was replaced by faradaic reactions which occur at the surface of the material.  The charge storage and kinetic benefits derived from using nanoscale metal oxides provide an interesting direction for the design of materials that offer both power d. and energy d.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq0ueeFhvSDZLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li_0UpfMlpA3w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2sXhtVChs7zL&amp;md5=b47809cb86f6cf28f5758e0eb3eac71e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1038/nmat2612"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Brezesinski, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tolbert, S.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ordered mesoporous α-MoO3 with iso-oriented nanocrystalline walls for thin-film pseudocapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Brezesinski, Torsten; Wang, John; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Capacitive energy storage is distinguished from other types of electrochem. energy storage by short charging times and the ability to deliver significantly more power than batteries.  A limitation to this technol. is its low energy d. and there is interest in exploring pseudo-capacitive materials where faradaic mechanisms offer increased energy storage.  The capacitive charge-storage properties of mesoporous films of iso-oriented α-MoO3 are superior to those of either mesoporous amorphous material or nonporous cryst. MoO3.  Whereas both cryst. and amorphous mesoporous materials show redox pseudo-capacitance, the iso-oriented layered cryst. domains enable Li ions to be inserted into the van der Waals gaps of the α-MoO3.  Probably this extra contribution arises from an intercalation pseudo-capacitance, which occurs on the same timescale as redox pseudo-capacitance.  The result is increased charge-storage capacity without compromising charge/discharge kinetics in mesoporous cryst. MoO3.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp77bOsasmjcrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li_0UpfMlpA3w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXhtVOnt78%253D&amp;md5=b6e743b60b27d6e0dfcabcf281d3d475</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms12122"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chao, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Savilov, S.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-assembled N-doped MoS2/carbon spheres by naturally occurring acid-catalyzed reaction for improved sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lim, Hyojun; Kim, Hyeongwoo; Kim, Sang-Ok; Choi, Wonchang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) has been considered a promising anode material for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) because of its relatively high theor. capacity and 2D-layered structure. In this study, nitrogen self-doped MoS2/carbon spheres (denoted as N-MoS2/C) were easily synthesized through a facile naturally occurring acid-catalyzed method, which takes advantage of the self-doping effect of thioacetamide as a sulfur as well as nitrogen co-source and the self-polymn. property of furfural as a carbon source.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A polymer-direct-intercalation strategy for MoS2/carbon-derived heteroaerogels with ultrahigh pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Feng Nan; Meng Ruijin; Zu Lianhai; Feng Yutong; Huang Jimei; Liu Guanglei; Chen Bingjie; Yang Jinhu; Feng Nan; Meng Ruijin; Yang Jinhu; Peng Chengxin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">The intercalation strategy has become crucial for 2D layered materials to achieve desirable properties, however, the intercalated guests are often limited to metal ions or small molecules.  Here, we develop a simple, mild and efficient polymer-direct-intercalation strategy that different polymers (polyethyleneimine and polyethylene glycol) can directly intercalate into the MoS2 interlayers, forming MoS(2)-polymer composites and interlayer-expanded MoS2/carbon heteroaerogels after carbonization.  The polymer-direct-intercalation behavior has been investigated by substantial characterizations and molecular dynamic calculations.  The resulting composite heteroaerogels possess 3D conductive MoS2/C frameworks, expanded MoS2 interlayers (0.98 nm), high MoS2 contents (up to 74%) and high Mo valence (+6), beneficial to fast and stable charge transport and enhanced pseudocapacitive energy storage.  Consequently, the typical MoS2/N-doped carbon heteroaerogels exhibit outstanding supercapacitor performance, such as ultrahigh capacitance, remarkable rate capability and excellent cycling stability.  This study offers a new intercalation strategy which may be generally applicable to 2D materials for promising energy applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcRfOvkUUbyTduIHSmpohpd0fW6udTcc2eYRmiMHJbHlebntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1016/j.ensm.2020.03.002</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D28%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D91-100%26journal%3DEnergy%2BStorage%2BMater.%26author%3DD.%2BXu%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DR.%2BQiu%26author%3DQ.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BMao%26author%3DY.%2BJiang%26author%3DR.%2BWang%26author%3DB.%2BHe%26author%3DY.%2BGong%26author%3DD.%2BLi%26title%3DCoupling%2Bof%2BBowl-Like%2BVS2%2BNanosheet%2BArrays%2Band%2BCarbon%2BNanofiber%2BEnables%2BUltrafast%2BNa%252B-Storage%2Band%2BRobust%2BFlexibility%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BHybrid%2BCapacitors%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.ensm.2020.03.002&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c05096&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.ensm.2020.03.002&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b12079"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Vertically Oxygen-Incorporated MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets Coated on Carbon Fibers for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">35206</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">35215</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.8b12079</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D35206-35215%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DH.%2BTao%26author%3DT.%2BLi%26author%3DS.%2BDu%26author%3DJ.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DX.%2BYang%26title%3DVertically%2BOxygen-Incorporated%2BMoS2%2BNanosheets%2BCoated%2Bon%2BCarbon%2BFibers%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.8b12079&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c05096&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.8b12079&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Vertically Oxygen-Incorporated MoS2 Nanosheets Coated on Carbon Fibers for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yaqiong; Tao, Huachao; Li, Tao; Du, Shaolin; Li, Jinhang; Zhang, Yukun; Yang, Xuelin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">35206-35215</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing a high-performance anode with high reversible capacity, rate performance, and great cycling stability is highly important for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  MoS2 has attracted extensive interest as the anode for SIBs.  Herein, the vertically oxygen-incorporated MoS2 nanosheets/carbon fibers are constructed via a facile hydrothermal method and then by simple calcination in air.  Oxygen incorporation into MoS2 can increase the defect degree and expand the interlayer spacing.  Vertical MoS2 nanosheet array coated on carbon fibers not only can expose rich active sites and reduce the diffusion distance of Na+, but also improve the electronic cond. and enhance structural stability.  Meanwhile, interlayer-expanded MoS2 can decrease Na+ diffusion resistance and increase accessible active sites for Na+.  In this work, the electrode combining the oxygen-incorporated strategy with vertical MoS2 nanosheet-integrated carbon fibers displays high specific capacities of 330 mAh g-1 over 100 cycles at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1 together with excellent rate behavior as the anode for SIBs.  This strategy offers a helpful way for improving the electrochem. performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpRocXiSvkTeLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgBtS9a8UU-rg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhslGqsrjI&amp;md5=b4d7b6f96048592aae4de944a9706cee</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit53" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.08.030"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Norouzi
Banis, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhanced Sodium Storage Capability Enabled by Super Wide-Interlayer-Spacing MoS<sub>2</sub> Integrated on Carbon Fibers</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>41</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">66</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">74</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.08.030</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D41%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D66-74%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DC.%2BZhao%26author%3DC.%2BYu%26author%3DM.%2BZhang%26author%3DQ.%2BSun%26author%3DS.%2BLi%26author%3DM.%2BNorouzi%250ABanis%26author%3DX.%2BHan%26author%3DQ.%2BDong%26author%3DJ.%2BYang%26author%3DG.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BSun%26author%3DJ.%2BQiu%26title%3DEnhanced%2BSodium%2BStorage%2BCapability%2BEnabled%2Bby%2BSuper%2BWide-Interlayer-Spacing%2BMoS2%2BIntegrated%2Bon%2BCarbon%2BFibers%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2017.08.030&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c05096&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2017.08.030&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced sodium storage capability enabled by super wide-interlayer-spacing MoS2 integrated on carbon fibers</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Changtai; Yu, Chang; Zhang, Mengdi; Sun, Qian; Li, Shaofeng; Norouzi Banis, Mohammad; Han, Xiaotong; Dong, Qiang; Yang, Juan; Wang, Gang; Sun, Xueliang; Qiu, Jieshan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">41</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">66-74</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing advanced electrode materials for effective pseudocapacitive charge storage is one of effective strategies to enhance the rate capability and cycling stability of sodium ion storage devices.  Herein, we fabricate MoS2 nanoflowers with super wide interlayer spacing (nearly twice as large as that of the original MoS2) supported on carbon fibers (named as E-MoS2/carbon fibers) and demonstrate its superior electrochem. performances as flexible and binder-free anodes for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) and sodium-ion hybrid capacitors (SIHCs).  Grafting MoS2 nanoflowers onto the carbon fiber networks not only ensures the fast electron transfer, but also endows it with flexible feature.  The super wide interlayer spacing of MoS2 nanoflowers can not only decrease the ion diffusion pathways and resistance, but also increase their available and accessible active surface area, thus guaranteeing the rapid mass transport.  Also, it can accommodate the large internal strain during discharge/charge processes.  Benefiting from these combined structure merits, the E-MoS2/carbon fibers electrodes deliver an ultralong cycling stability up to 3000 cycles and the superior rate capacity of 104 mA h g-1 at 20 A g-1, which just takes ca. 18.7 s to fully charge/discharge.  When further employed as the anode for SIHCs, it delivers high energy and power densities due to the high pseudocapacitive charge storage of the super wide interlayer spacing E-MoS2/carbon fibers.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGom_c5ywhsXr7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgBtS9a8UU-rg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsFCltL7K&amp;md5=5ac9c7c8f86744dee8f08118939281b5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54'); <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bundled Defect-Rich MoS<sub>2</sub> for a High-Rate and Long-Life Sodium-Ion Battery: Achieving 3D Diffusion of Sodium Ion by Vacancies to Improve Kinetics</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>15</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">e1805405</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/smll.201805405</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D15%26publication_year%3D2019%26journal%3DSmall%26author%3DK.%2BYao%26author%3DZ.%2BXu%26author%3DJ.%2BHuang%26author%3DM.%2BMa%26author%3DL.%2BFu%26author%3DX.%2BShen%26author%3DJ.%2BLi%26author%3DM.%2BFu%26title%3DBundled%2BDefect-Rich%2BMoS2%2Bfor%2Ba%2BHigh-Rate%2Band%2BLong-Life%2BSodium-Ion%2BBattery%253A%2BAchieving%2B3D%2BDiffusion%2Bof%2BSodium%2BIon%2Bby%2BVacancies%2Bto%2BImprove%2BKinetics%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fsmll.201805405&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c05096&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fsmll.201805405&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrical Energy Storage for the Grid: A Battery of Choices</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dunn, Bruce; Kamath, Haresh; Tarascon, Jean-Marie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science (Washington, DC, United States)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The increasing interest in energy storage for the grid can be attributed to multiple factors, including the capital costs of managing peak demands, the investments needed for grid reliability, and the integration of renewable energy sources.  Although existing energy storage is dominated by pumped hydroelec., there is the recognition that battery systems can offer a no. of high-value opportunities, provided that lower costs can be obtained.  The battery systems reviewed here include sodium-sulfur batteries that are com. available for grid applications, redox-flow batteries that offer low cost, and lithium-ion batteries whose development for com. electronics and elec. vehicles is being applied to grid storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrZwDymuubZm7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liD6RLxNXpVJA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhsVGktL%252FJ&amp;md5=5035bfda7631ad9d075e8836e61146ef</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201803609"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.
